================================================================================
DOCUMENT OVERVIEW
================================================================================

This document provides complete end-to-end implementation of an enterprise-grade
Jenkins automation platform with dual Ansible versions (2.9 + 6.7) for unified
OS patching across Ubuntu 22/24 and Oracle Linux 8/9.

PLATFORM CAPABILITIES:
- Jenkins 2.479.2 LTS with HTTPS (NGINX reverse proxy)
- Dual Ansible architecture: 2.9 (system) + 6.7 (virtual environment)
- Unified OS patching for Ubuntu 22, Ubuntu 24, Oracle Linux 8, Oracle 9
- Dual-firewall architecture (iptables for Ubuntu, firewalld for Oracle)
- Service account automation (svc_ans)
- LDAP integration support
- Production-grade security hardening
- Comprehensive backup and recovery
- Enterprise monitoring and troubleshooting

INFRASTRUCTURE DETAILS:
- Control Node: 192.168.121.182 jenkinspreprod.local (Oracle Linux 8.10)
- Ubuntu 22    : 192.168.68.110  ubuntu22.local     (Ubuntu 22.04 LTS)
- Ubuntu 24    : 192.168.121.164 ubuntu24.local     (Ubuntu 24.04 LTS)
- Oracle 8     : 192.168.121.150 oracle8.local      (Oracle Linux 8.10)
- Oracle 9     : 192.168.121.177 oracle9.local      (Oracle Linux 9.5)

SOFTWARE VERSIONS:
- Jenkins      : 2.479.2 LTS
- Java         : 21.0.5 (OpenJDK)
- NGINX        : 1.20.1
- Python       : 3.11.9 (control node)
- Ansible      : 2.9.27 (system) + 6.7.0 (virtual environment)

NETWORK PORTS:
- 22   : SSH (all nodes)
- 443  : HTTPS (Jenkins web UI)
- 8080 : Jenkins internal (localhost only)

USER ACCOUNTS:
- root     : System administrator
- jenkins  : Jenkins service account (UID ~994)
- svc_ans  : Ansible automation service account (UID 1001)

FIREWALL ENGINES:
- Control Node    : firewalld
- Ubuntu Nodes    : iptables + netfilter-persistent
- Oracle Nodes    : firewalld

PART 1: INFRASTRUCTURE PREPARATION
================================================================================

This section prepares all nodes (control node and managed nodes) with proper
hostname configuration, name resolution, time synchronization, and system
updates.

PREREQUISITES:
- Root or sudo access on all nodes
- Network connectivity between all nodes
- Internet access for package downloads


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1.1: HOSTNAME CONFIGURATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Set proper hostnames on all nodes for consistent identification

EXECUTION: Run commands on respective nodes as root


On Control Node (192.168.121.182):
-----------------------------------

hostnamectl set-hostname jenkinspreprod.local
hostnamectl

# Verify output:
#   Static hostname: jenkinspreprod.local
#   Icon name: computer-vm
#   Chassis: vm
#   Machine ID: <machine-id>
#   Boot ID: <boot-id>
#   Virtualization: kvm
#   Operating System: Oracle Linux Server 8.10
#   Kernel: Linux 5.x.x
#   Architecture: x86-64


On Managed Nodes:
-----------------

# Ubuntu 22 (192.168.68.110)
hostnamectl set-hostname ubuntu22.local
hostnamectl

# Ubuntu 24 (192.168.121.164)
hostnamectl set-hostname ubuntu24.local
hostnamectl

# Oracle 8 (192.168.121.150)
hostnamectl set-hostname oracle8.local
hostnamectl

# Oracle 9 (192.168.121.177)
hostnamectl set-hostname oracle9.local
hostnamectl


VERIFICATION:
-------------

# On each node, verify hostname:
hostname
# Expected: <hostname>.local

# Verify FQDN:
hostname -f
# Expected: <hostname>.local


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1.2: /ETC/HOSTS CONFIGURATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Configure local name resolution for all nodes to communicate by hostname

EXECUTION: Run commands on respective nodes as root

IMPORTANT: These entries enable DNS-independent hostname resolution


On Control Node (jenkinspreprod.local - 192.168.121.182):
----------------------------------------------------------

cat >> /etc/hosts << 'EOF'
127.0.0.1       localhost
127.0.1.1       jenkinspreprod.local jenkinspreprod
192.168.121.182 jenkinspreprod.local jenkinspreprod
192.168.121.152 ubuntu22.local ubuntu22
192.168.121.164 ubuntu24.local ubuntu24
192.168.121.150 oracle8.local oracle8
192.168.121.177 oracle9.local oracle9
EOF

# Verify entries:
cat /etc/hosts

# Test resolution:
ping -c 2 ubuntu22.local
ping -c 2 ubuntu24.local
ping -c 2 oracle8.local
ping -c 2 oracle9.local


On Ubuntu 22 (192.168.68.110):
-------------------------------

cat >> /etc/hosts << 'EOF'
127.0.0.1       localhost
127.0.1.1       ubuntu22.local ubuntu22
192.168.121.152  ubuntu22.local ubuntu22
192.168.121.182 jenkinspreprod.local jenkinspreprod
192.168.121.164 ubuntu24.local ubuntu24
192.168.121.150 oracle8.local oracle8
192.168.121.177 oracle9.local oracle9
EOF

# Verify entries:
cat /etc/hosts

# Test resolution:
ping -c 2 jenkinspreprod.local


On Ubuntu 24 (192.168.121.164):
--------------------------------

cat >> /etc/hosts << 'EOF'
127.0.0.1       localhost
127.0.1.1       ubuntu24.local ubuntu24
192.168.121.164 ubuntu24.local ubuntu24
192.168.121.182 jenkinspreprod.local jenkinspreprod
192.168.121.152 ubuntu22.local ubuntu22
192.168.121.150 oracle8.local oracle8
192.168.121.177 oracle9.local oracle9
EOF

# Verify entries:
cat /etc/hosts

# Test resolution:
ping -c 2 jenkinspreprod.local


On Oracle 8 (192.168.121.150):
-------------------------------

cat >> /etc/hosts << 'EOF'

127.0.1.1       oracle8.local oracle8

192.168.121.182 jenkinspreprod.local jenkinspreprod

# Verify entries:

-------------------------------

VERIFICATION CHECKLIST:
-----------------------

# From control node, verify connectivity to all managed nodes:
for host in ubuntu22.local ubuntu24.local oracle8.local oracle9.local; do
    echo "Testing $host..."
    ping -c 2 $host
done

# Expected: All pings successful (0% packet loss)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1.3: TIME SYNCHRONIZATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Ensure all nodes have synchronized time for accurate logging and 
         certificate validation

EXECUTION: Run commands on respective nodes as root


On Control Node and Oracle Linux Nodes (Using Chrony):
-------------------------------------------------------

# Install chrony
dnf install -y chrony

# Configure chrony with multiple reliable NTP sources
cat > /etc/chrony.conf << 'EOF'
# Public NTP servers
pool time.google.com iburst
pool 0.pool.ntp.org iburst
pool 1.pool.ntp.org iburst
pool 2.pool.ntp.org iburst
pool 3.pool.ntp.org iburst

# Drift file
driftfile /var/lib/chrony/drift

# Allow large time corrections
makestep 1.0 3

# Enable kernel synchronization
rtcsync

# Key file for chronyc authentication
keyfile /etc/chrony.keys

# Leap second timezone
leapsectz right/UTC

# Log directory
logdir /var/log/chrony
EOF

# Enable and start chronyd
systemctl enable chronyd
systemctl start chronyd

# Verify chrony is tracking time
chronyc tracking

# Expected output:
# Reference ID    : <NTP server IP>
# Stratum         : 2 or 3
# Ref time (UTC)  : <current time>
# System time     : 0.000000001 seconds fast/slow of NTP time
# Last offset     : +/-0.000XXXXXX seconds
# RMS offset      : 0.000XXXXXX seconds
# Frequency       : X.XXX ppm slow/fast
# Residual freq   : +/-X.XXX ppm
# Skew            : X.XXX ppm
# Root delay      : 0.0XXXXXXX seconds
# Root dispersion : 0.00XXXXXX seconds
# Update interval : XX.X seconds
# Leap status     : Normal

# Verify NTP sources
chronyc sources -v

# Expected: Multiple sources listed with ^ or * indicating synchronization


On Ubuntu Nodes (Using systemd-timesyncd):
-------------------------------------------

# Enable NTP synchronization
timedatectl set-ntp true

# Configure timesyncd with reliable NTP sources
cat > /etc/systemd/timesyncd.conf << 'EOF'
[Time]
NTP=time.google.com 0.pool.ntp.org 1.pool.ntp.org
FallbackNTP=time.cloudflare.com 2.pool.ntp.org 3.pool.ntp.org
EOF

# Restart timesyncd service
systemctl restart systemd-timesyncd

# Verify time synchronization status
timedatectl status

# Expected output:
#                Local time: <current local time>
#            Universal time: <current UTC time>
#                  RTC time: <hardware clock time>
#                 Time zone: <your timezone>
# System clock synchronized: yes
#               NTP service: active
#           RTC in local TZ: no

# Check timesyncd status
systemctl status systemd-timesyncd

# Expected: active (running)


VERIFICATION:
-------------

# On each node, verify time synchronization:
timedatectl status | grep "synchronized"
# Expected: System clock synchronized: yes

# Verify all nodes have similar time (within 1 second):
date
# Compare times across all nodes


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1.4: SYSTEM UPDATES
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Update all packages to latest versions for security and stability

EXECUTION: Run commands on respective nodes as root

WARNING: System updates may require a reboot. Plan accordingly.


On Oracle Linux Nodes (Control Node, Oracle 8, Oracle 9):
----------------------------------------------------------

# Clean yum/dnf cache
dnf clean all

# Update all packages
dnf update -y

# Expected output:
# ... (list of packages to be updated)
# Complete!

dnf install -y dnf-utils
apt install -y needrestart

# Check if reboot is required
needs-restarting -r

ls /var/run/reboot-required
cat /var/run/reboot-required.pkgs

# Expected output:
# Core libraries or services have been updated:
#   kernel -> reboot is required
# OR
# No core libraries or services have been updated.
# Reboot is not necessary.

# If reboot required:
# reboot

# After reboot, verify system:
# uptime
# uname -r  # Verify new kernel is running


On Ubuntu Nodes (Ubuntu 22, Ubuntu 24):
----------------------------------------

# Update package lists
apt update

# Upgrade all packages
apt upgrade -y

# Expected output:
# ... (list of packages to be upgraded)
# Processing triggers for ...
# Done.

# Perform distribution upgrade (if needed)
apt dist-upgrade -y

# Remove unnecessary packages
apt autoremove -y
apt autoclean

# Check if reboot is required
if [ -f /var/run/reboot-required ]; then
    echo "Reboot required"
    cat /var/run/reboot-required.pkgs
else
    echo "No reboot required"
fi

# If reboot required:
# reboot

# After reboot, verify system:
# uptime
# uname -r  # Verify new kernel is running


VERIFICATION CHECKLIST:
-----------------------

# On all nodes:
uname -a
# Verify kernel version

# Check system uptime after reboot:
uptime

# Verify no broken packages (Ubuntu):
apt --fix-broken install

# Verify no issues (Oracle Linux):
dnf check


POST-UPDATE TASKS:
------------------

# Verify critical services are running after reboot:

# On control node:
systemctl status chronyd
systemctl status sshd

# On all nodes:
systemctl status sshd
systemctl status systemd-timesyncd  # Ubuntu
systemctl status chronyd            # Oracle Linux


IMPORTANT NOTES:
----------------

1. System updates should be performed during maintenance windows
2. Always verify services restart correctly after reboot
3. Document kernel versions before and after updates
4. Test connectivity after reboot before proceeding


================================================================================
PART 2: JENKINS INSTALLATION & CONFIGURATION
================================================================================

This section installs and configures Jenkins LTS on the control node with
production-grade settings.

PREREQUISITES:
- Control node fully prepared (Part 1 completed)
- Root or sudo access on control node
- Internet connectivity for package downloads

CRITICAL NOTES:
- Use rpm-stable repository URL (NOT redhat-stable)
- Install Java 21 BEFORE Jenkins
- Jenkins will listen on localhost:8080 only (NGINX will handle external access)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.1: PRE-REQUISITES
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Install required tools for Jenkins installation

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root


# Install wget for downloading repository files
yum install -y wget

# Verify wget installation
which wget
# Expected: /usr/bin/wget

wget --version
# Expected: GNU Wget 1.x.x


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.2: JENKINS REPOSITORY SETUP
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Configure Jenkins LTS repository for installation

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root

CRITICAL: Use rpm-stable URL to avoid "No match for argument: jenkins" error


# Step 1: Download Jenkins repository file
wget -O /etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo \
    https://pkg.jenkins.io/rpm-stable/jenkins.repo

# Expected output:
# Saving to: '/etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo'
# ... 100%

# Step 2: Verify repository file contains [jenkins] block (NOT HTML)
cat /etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo

# Expected output:
# [jenkins]
# name=Jenkins-stable
# baseurl=http://pkg.jenkins.io/redhat-stable
# gpgcheck=1

# WARNING: If output shows HTML content, repository download failed
# Re-run wget command with correct URL


# Step 3: Import Jenkins GPG key
rpm --import https://pkg.jenkins.io/rpm-stable/jenkins.io-2023.key

# Expected: No output (success)

# Verify GPG key imported
rpm -q gpg-pubkey --qf '%{NAME}-%{VERSION}-%{RELEASE}\t%{SUMMARY}\n' | grep -i jenkins

# Expected output showing Jenkins GPG key


TROUBLESHOOTING:
----------------

# If "No match for argument: jenkins" error occurs during installation:
# 1. Verify repository file contains [jenkins] block:
cat /etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo

# 2. If HTML content found, delete and re-download:
rm /etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo
wget -O /etc/yum.repos.d/jenkins.repo \
    https://pkg.jenkins.io/rpm-stable/jenkins.repo

# 3. Verify repository is recognized:
yum repolist | grep -i jenkins
# Expected: jenkins/x86_64    Jenkins-stable


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.3: JAVA 21 INSTALLATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Install Java 21 (required for Jenkins 2.479.2 LTS)

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root

CRITICAL: Java 21 MUST be installed BEFORE Jenkins


# Step 1: Upgrade all packages first
yum upgrade -y

# Step 2: Install fontconfig (required by Java)
yum install -y fontconfig

# Step 3: Install Java 21 OpenJDK and development tools
yum install -y java-21-openjdk java-21-openjdk-devel

# Expected output:
# ... Installing: java-21-openjdk
# ... Installing: java-21-openjdk-devel
# Complete!


# Step 4: Verify Java 21 installation
java -version

# Expected output:
# openjdk version "21.0.5" 2024-10-15 LTS
# OpenJDK Runtime Environment (Red_Hat-21.0.5.0.11-1) (build 21.0.5+11-LTS)
# OpenJDK 64-Bit Server VM (Red_Hat-21.0.5.0.11-1) (build 21.0.5+11-LTS, mixed mode, sharing)


# Step 5: If multiple Java versions exist, set Java 21 as default
alternatives --config java

# Output will show:
# There are X programs which provide 'java'.
#
#   Selection    Command
# -----------------------------------------------
#    1           /usr/lib/jvm/java-11-openjdk/bin/java
# *+ 2           /usr/lib/jvm/java-21-openjdk/bin/java
#
# Enter to keep the current selection[+], or type selection number:

# Type the number corresponding to java-21-openjdk and press Enter

# Step 6: Verify Java 21 is active
java -version | head -1
# Expected: openjdk version "21.0.5"

which java
# Expected: /usr/bin/java

readlink -f /usr/bin/java
# Expected: /usr/lib/jvm/java-21-openjdk-21.0.5.0.11-1.el8.x86_64/bin/java


VERIFICATION:
-------------

# Verify JAVA_HOME (if needed by applications)
echo $JAVA_HOME

# If not set, add to /etc/environment:
echo 'JAVA_HOME=/usr/lib/jvm/java-21-openjdk' >> /etc/environment
source /etc/environment
echo $JAVA_HOME
# Expected: /usr/lib/jvm/java-21-openjdk

SECTION 2.4: JENKINS INSTALLATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Install Jenkins LTS package

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root


# Install Jenkins
yum install -y jenkins

# Expected output:
# ... Installing: jenkins-2.479.2-1.1

rpm -qa | grep jenkins
# Expected: jenkins-2.479.2-1.1.noarch

JENKINS FILES AND DIRECTORIES:
-------------------------------

After installation, Jenkins creates:

/usr/bin/jenkins              # Jenkins executable
/var/lib/jenkins/             # Jenkins home directory (JENKINS_HOME)
/var/log/jenkins/             # Jenkins logs
/var/cache/jenkins/           # Jenkins cache
/etc/sysconfig/jenkins        # Jenkins configuration file
/usr/lib/systemd/system/jenkins.service  # Systemd service unit


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.5: JENKINS SYSTEMD CONFIGURATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Configure Jenkins to listen on localhost only with production settings

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root

SECURITY: Jenkins listens on 127.0.0.1:8080 (localhost only)
          NGINX will handle external HTTPS connections


# Create systemd override directory
mkdir -p /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d

# Create override configuration
cat > /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d/override.conf << 'EOF'
[Service]
# Clear existing ExecStart
ExecStart=

# Set new ExecStart with jenkins binary
ExecStart=/usr/bin/jenkins

# Java options
Environment="JAVA_OPTS=-Djava.awt.headless=true -Xmx2048m -Xms1024m"

# Jenkins options - LISTEN ON LOCALHOST ONLY
Environment="JENKINS_OPTS=--httpListenAddress=127.0.0.1 --httpPort=8080"

# Run as jenkins user
User=jenkins
Group=jenkins

# Security hardening
NoNewPrivileges=true
PrivateTmp=true

# Restart policy
Restart=on-failure
RestartSec=10s
EOF

# Verify override file created
cat /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d/override.conf


CONFIGURATION EXPLANATION:
--------------------------

JAVA_OPTS:
  -Djava.awt.headless=true : Run Java in headless mode (no GUI)
  -Xmx2048m                 : Maximum heap size 2GB
  -Xms1024m                 : Initial heap size 1GB

JENKINS_OPTS:
  --httpListenAddress=127.0.0.1 : Listen on localhost ONLY (security)
  --httpPort=8080               : Port 8080 (default)

Security:
  NoNewPrivileges=true : Prevent privilege escalation
  PrivateTmp=true      : Use private /tmp directory

Restart:
  Restart=on-failure   : Auto-restart on failure
  RestartSec=10s       : Wait 10 seconds before restart


# Reload systemd to apply override
systemctl daemon-reload

# Verify systemd configuration
systemctl cat jenkins.service | grep -A 20 "override.conf"


===================================

sudo mkdir -p /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d && sudo tee /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d/override.conf > /dev/null << 'EOF'
[Service]
# Clear the upstream ExecStart before overriding
ExecStart=
ExecStart=/usr/bin/jenkins
# ── JVM & Jenkins options ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Environment="JAVA_OPTS=\
  -Djava.awt.headless=true \
  -Xms4g -Xmx8g \
  -XX:+UseG1GC \
  -XX:MaxGCPauseMillis=200 \
  -XX:+ExplicitGCInvokesConcurrent \
  -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError \
  -XX:HeapDumpPath=/var/lib/jenkins/heap-dump/heap-dump.hprof \
  -Djava.net.preferIPv4Stack=true"
Environment="JENKINS_OPTS=\
  --httpListenAddress=127.0.0.1 \
  --httpPort=8080"
# ── Identity ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
User=jenkins
Group=jenkins
# ── Logging ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
StandardOutput=journal
StandardError=journal
SyslogIdentifier=jenkins
# ── Startup / Shutdown ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
TimeoutStartSec=300
TimeoutStopSec=120
Restart=on-failure
RestartSec=10s
# ── Resource limits ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
LimitNOFILE=65536
LimitNPROC=65536
LimitCORE=infinity
# ── Security hardening ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
NoNewPrivileges=true
PrivateTmp=true
ProtectSystem=full
ProtectHome=true
ProtectKernelTunables=true
ProtectKernelModules=true
ProtectControlGroups=true
RestrictAddressFamilies=AF_INET AF_INET6 AF_UNIX
LockPersonality=true
MemoryDenyWriteExecute=false
EOF

sudo systemctl status jenkins
sudo systemctl show jenkins | grep -E 'LimitNOFILE|MemoryDeny|ExecStart'


 
JVM OPTIONS (JAVA_OPTS)
  -Djava.awt.headless=true          No GUI — required for server environments.
  -Xms4g                            JVM starts with 4 GB heap allocated.
  -Xmx8g                            JVM can grow up to 8 GB heap max.
  -XX:+UseG1GC                      Use G1 garbage collector (best for large heaps).
  -XX:MaxGCPauseMillis=200          Target GC pauses under 200 ms.
  -XX:+ExplicitGCInvokesConcurrent  System.gc() runs concurrently (less disruptive).
  -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError   Auto-dump heap on OOM for post-mortem analysis.
  -XX:HeapDumpPath=...              Where to write the heap dump file.
  -Djava.net.preferIPv4Stack=true   Force IPv4 — avoids IPv6 DNS issues.
 
JENKINS OPTIONS (JENKINS_OPTS)
  --httpListenAddress=127.0.0.1     Only accept connections from localhost
                                    (put a reverse proxy like nginx in front).
  --httpPort=8080                   Listen on port 8080.
 
RESOURCE LIMITS
  LimitNOFILE=65536   Max open file descriptors (Jenkins opens many files).
  LimitNPROC=65536    Max processes/threads the jenkins user can spawn.
  LimitCORE=infinity  Unlimited core dump size (useful for debugging crashes).
 
SECURITY HARDENING
  NoNewPrivileges=true          The process cannot gain new Linux capabilities.
  PrivateTmp=true               Jenkins gets its own isolated /tmp directory.
  ProtectSystem=full            /usr, /boot, /etc are read-only to the service.
  ProtectHome=true              /home, /root, /run/user are hidden.
  ProtectKernelTunables=true    Cannot write to /proc/sys kernel parameters.
  ProtectKernelModules=true     Cannot load or unload kernel modules.
  ProtectControlGroups=true     Cannot modify cgroup hierarchy.
  RestrictAddressFamilies=...   Only IPv4, IPv6, and Unix sockets allowed.
  LockPersonality=true          Cannot change the execution domain.
  MemoryDenyWriteExecute=false  Allow JVM JIT (JIT needs write+exec memory).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.6: SET PERMISSIONS AND START JENKINS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Set proper ownership and start Jenkins service

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root


# Set ownership of Jenkins home directory
chown -R jenkins:jenkins /var/lib/jenkins
chmod 750 /var/lib/jenkins

# Verify permissions
ls -ld /var/lib/jenkins
# Expected: drwxr-x--- jenkins jenkins /var/lib/jenkins


# Enable Jenkins to start on boot
systemctl enable jenkins

# Expected output:
# Created symlink /etc/systemd/system/multi-user.target.wants/jenkins.service


# Start Jenkins service
systemctl start jenkins

# Wait 30 seconds for Jenkins to fully start
sleep 30

# Check Jenkins status
systemctl status jenkins

# Expected output:
# ● jenkins.service - Jenkins Continuous Integration Server
#    Loaded: loaded (/usr/lib/systemd/system/jenkins.service; enabled; vendor preset: disabled)
#   Drop-In: /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d
#            └─override.conf
#    Active: active (running) since <timestamp>
#  Main PID: <pid> (java)
#     Tasks: <number>
#    Memory: <usage>
#    CGroup: /system.slice/jenkins.service
#            └─<pid> /usr/bin/java -Djava.awt.headless=true ...


# Verify Jenkins is listening on localhost:8080
ss -tlnp | grep 8080

# Expected output:
# LISTEN   0   50   [::ffff:127.0.0.1]:8080   *:*   users:(("java",pid=<pid>,fd=<fd>))

# This confirms Jenkins listens on 127.0.0.1:8080 ONLY (localhost)


# Check Jenkins logs
journalctl -u jenkins -n 50

# Look for:
# Jenkins is fully up and running
# No error messages


TROUBLESHOOTING:
----------------

# If Jenkins fails to start:

# Check logs:
journalctl -u jenkins -n 100 --no-pager

# Common issues:
# 1. Java not found: Verify Java 21 installed
# 2. Port 8080 in use: Check with ss -tlnp | grep 8080
# 3. Permissions: Verify /var/lib/jenkins owned by jenkins user

# Restart Jenkins:
systemctl restart jenkins
systemctl status jenkins


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2.7: GET INITIAL PASSWORD
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Retrieve Jenkins initial admin password for first-time setup

EXECUTION: Run commands on control node as root


# Retrieve initial password
cat /var/lib/jenkins/secrets/initialAdminPassword

# Expected output (example):
# 9ca4359de7944920b9463b387cf5036b

# IMPORTANT: Save this password - you'll need it for Jenkins web setup


# CRITICAL: Fix SELinux to allow NGINX proxy to Jenkins
setsebool -P httpd_can_network_connect 1

# Verify SELinux boolean is enabled
getsebool httpd_can_network_connect

# Expected output:
# httpd_can_network_connect --> on

# This allows NGINX to connect to Jenkins on localhost:8080


VERIFICATION CHECKLIST:
-----------------------

[ ] Jenkins service running: systemctl status jenkins
[ ] Jenkins listening on 127.0.0.1:8080: ss -tlnp | grep 8080
[ ] Initial password retrieved: cat /var/lib/jenkins/secrets/initialAdminPassword
[ ] SELinux boolean enabled: getsebool httpd_can_network_connect
[ ] No errors in logs: journalctl -u jenkins -n 50


NEXT STEPS:
-----------

Before accessing Jenkins web UI:
1. Install and configure NGINX reverse proxy (Part 3)
2. Configure firewall to allow HTTPS (Part 4)
3. Access Jenkins at https://jenkinspreprod.local
4. Complete Jenkins initial setup wizard


IMPORTANT NOTES:
----------------

1. Jenkins is NOT accessible externally yet (localhost only)
2. NGINX reverse proxy will provide HTTPS access
3. Initial password is stored in /var/lib/jenkins/secrets/initialAdminPassword
4. Password file is deleted after first admin user is created
5. Jenkins home directory: /var/lib/jenkins/
