SECTION 13.4: BACKUP TESTING AND VERIFICATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Regularly test backup and restore procedures

EXECUTION: Perform quarterly or after major changes


Test 1: Manual Backup Execution
--------------------------------

# Execute backup script manually
/usr/local/bin/backup-jenkins-ansible.sh

# Verify backup completed
ls -la /backup/ | tail -10

# Check backup manifest
cat /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-*/MANIFEST.txt

# Verify backup size reasonable
du -sh /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-*


Test 2: Restore Test (Non-Production Environment)
--------------------------------------------------

# Prerequisites: Test on separate system or VM

# Copy backup to test system
scp -r /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/ testhost:/tmp/

# On test host, execute restore
cd /tmp/jenkins-ansible-daily-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/
./RESTORE.sh

# Verify services start
systemctl status jenkins
systemctl status nginx

# Test Jenkins UI access
curl -k https://localhost

# Verify Ansible works
ansible all -m ping


Test 3: File Integrity Check
-----------------------------

# Extract and verify critical files
cd /tmp
tar tzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-*/jenkins-home.tar.gz | head -20
tar tzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-*/ansible-config.tar.gz | head -20

# Verify no corruption
tar tzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-*/jenkins-home.tar.gz > /dev/null
echo $?
# Expected: 0 (no errors)


Test 4: Recovery Time Objective (RTO) Test
-------------------------------------------

# Time the restore process
time ./RESTORE.sh

# Document RTO
# Target RTO: < 30 minutes for full restore


BACKUP VERIFICATION CHECKLIST:
-------------------------------

[ ] Backup script executes without errors
[ ] All critical files backed up
[ ] Backup manifest created
[ ] Restore script generated
[ ] Backup size reasonable (not empty, not excessive)
[ ] Sensitive files encrypted (SSH keys, SSL certs)
[ ] Permissions set correctly (700 for backup dir)
[ ] Old backups cleaned up automatically
[ ] Offsite copy created (if configured)
[ ] Backup log created
[ ] Email notification sent (if configured)
[ ] Restore test successful (quarterly)
[ ] RTO within acceptable limits


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 13.5: DISASTER RECOVERY PROCEDURES
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Step-by-step disaster recovery guide

SCENARIOS:


Scenario 1: Jenkins Corruption or Failure
------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Jenkins fails to start
- Jenkins UI not accessible
- Configuration errors

Recovery Steps:

1. Stop Jenkins:
   systemctl stop jenkins

2. Backup current state (if possible):
   mv /var/lib/jenkins /var/lib/jenkins.broken

3. Restore from backup:
   cd /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/
   tar xzf jenkins-home.tar.gz -C /

4. Fix permissions:
   chown -R jenkins:jenkins /var/lib/jenkins
   chmod 750 /var/lib/jenkins

5. Start Jenkins:
   systemctl start jenkins

6. Verify:
   systemctl status jenkins
   curl -k https://jenkinspreprod.local


Scenario 2: Complete System Loss
---------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Hardware failure
- OS corruption
- Catastrophic failure

Recovery Steps:

1. Rebuild system:
   - Install Oracle Linux 8.10
   - Configure hostname and network
   - Update system

2. Restore backup:
   - Copy latest backup from offsite storage
   - Extract to temporary location

3. Execute restore script:
   cd /path/to/backup/
   ./RESTORE.sh

4. Reinstall software if needed:
   - Java 21
   - Jenkins
   - NGINX
   - Ansible

5. Restore configurations:
   - Already done by RESTORE.sh

6. Verify all services:
   systemctl status jenkins nginx firewalld

7. Test end-to-end:
   - Access Jenkins UI
   - Run Ansible ping test
   - Execute test pipeline


Scenario 3: Lost SSH Keys
--------------------------

Symptoms:
- Cannot SSH to managed nodes
- Ansible automation fails

Recovery Steps:

1. Stop Jenkins (prevent failed executions):
   systemctl stop jenkins

2. Restore SSH keys from backup:
   tar xzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-*/ssh-keys.tar.gz -C /

3. Fix permissions:
   chown -R svc_ans:svc_ans /home/svc_ans/.ssh
   chmod 700 /home/svc_ans/.ssh
   chmod 600 /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa
   chmod 644 /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa.pub

4. Test SSH:
   su - svc_ans
   ssh 192.168.68.110 hostname

5. Start Jenkins:
   systemctl start jenkins


Scenario 4: NGINX Configuration Loss
-------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- NGINX fails to start
- 502 Bad Gateway errors
- Configuration syntax errors

Recovery Steps:

1. Stop NGINX:
   systemctl stop nginx

2. Restore configuration:
   tar xzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-*/nginx-config.tar.gz -C /

3. Test configuration:
   nginx -t

4. Start NGINX:
   systemctl start nginx

5. Verify:
   curl -k -I https://jenkinspreprod.local


DISASTER RECOVERY BEST PRACTICES:
----------------------------------

1. Regular Testing:
   - Test restore quarterly
   - Document actual RTO
   - Update procedures based on tests

2. Documentation:
   - Keep printed copy of recovery procedures
   - Store offsite with backups
   - Include contact information

3. Backup Verification:
   - Automated verification after each backup
   - Manual verification monthly
   - Test restore on non-production system

4. Offsite Storage:
   - Daily sync to offsite location
   - Geographic separation
   - Encrypted transfer and storage

5. Communication Plan:
   - Defined escalation path
   - Emergency contact list
   - Status update procedures

6. Recovery Time Objectives:
   - RTO: < 4 hours for full recovery
   - RPO: < 24 hours (daily backups)
   - Document actual times during tests


BACKUP AND RECOVERY SUMMARY:
-----------------------------

✓ Comprehensive backup script created
✓ Automated scheduling configured
✓ Restore procedures documented
✓ Disaster recovery scenarios covered
✓ Testing procedures defined
✓ Retention policy established
✓ Offsite backup capability
✓ Verification procedures in place


NEXT STEPS:
-----------

1. Test backup script execution
2. Verify cron schedule
3. Perform initial restore test
4. Document actual RTO/RPO
5. Configure offsite storage
6. Set up monitoring (Part 14)

SECTION 14.1: SERVICE MONITORING
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Monitor critical services and system health

EXECUTION: Regular monitoring procedures


DAILY MONITORING TASKS:
-----------------------

Jenkins Service Monitoring:
---------------------------

# Check Jenkins status
systemctl status jenkins

# Expected output:
# ● jenkins.service - Jenkins Continuous Integration Server
#    Loaded: loaded (/usr/lib/systemd/system/jenkins.service; enabled)
#    Active: active (running) since ...
#    Memory: <usage>MB


# Check Jenkins is listening
ss -tlnp | grep 8080

# Expected output:
# LISTEN 0 50 [::ffff:127.0.0.1]:8080 *:* users:(("java",pid=...))


# Check Jenkins logs for errors
journalctl -u jenkins -n 50 | grep -i error

# If errors found, investigate further
journalctl -u jenkins -n 200 --no-pager


# Check Jenkins disk space
df -h /var/lib/jenkins

# Expected: < 80% usage
# Action if > 80%: Clean workspace, old builds


# Check Jenkins memory usage
ps aux | grep jenkins | grep -v grep

# Monitor %MEM column
# Expected: < 80% of allocated memory (2GB)


NGINX Service Monitoring:
--------------------------

# Check NGINX status
systemctl status nginx

# Expected output:
# ● nginx.service - The nginx HTTP and reverse proxy server
#    Active: active (running) since ...


# Check NGINX is listening on correct ports
ss -tlnp | grep nginx

# Expected output:
# LISTEN 0 511 0.0.0.0:80 *:* users:(("nginx",pid=...))
# LISTEN 0 511 0.0.0.0:443 *:* users:(("nginx",pid=...))


# Check NGINX error logs
tail -50 /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log

# Expected: No critical errors
# Warnings acceptable if not frequent


# Check NGINX access logs
tail -50 /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log

# Monitor for:
# - Excessive 502 errors (backend down)
# - Excessive 403/404 errors (misconfiguration)
# - Unusual traffic patterns


# Test NGINX configuration
nginx -t

# Expected output:
# nginx: the configuration file /etc/nginx/nginx.conf syntax is ok
# nginx: configuration file /etc/nginx/nginx.conf test is successful


Firewall Monitoring:
--------------------

# Check firewalld status (control node)
firewall-cmd --state

# Expected: running


# Verify firewall rules
firewall-cmd --list-all

# Expected: ssh and https services allowed


# Check fail2ban status
systemctl status fail2ban
fail2ban-client status sshd

# Monitor banned IPs
# Expected: Legitimate traffic not banned


# Check iptables on Ubuntu nodes
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "iptables -L -n -v"

# Verify rules present and counters incrementing


System Resource Monitoring:
----------------------------

# CPU usage
top -bn1 | head -20

# Monitor jenkins and nginx processes
# Expected: < 80% CPU usage


# Memory usage
free -h

# Expected: Sufficient free/available memory


# Disk space
df -h

# Critical filesystems:
# / (root)
# /var/lib/jenkins
# /home/svc_ans
# /backup

# Expected: All < 80% usage
# Alert if any > 90%


# Disk I/O
iostat -x 1 3

# Monitor for high %util
# Expected: < 80% utilization


# Network connectivity
ping -c 4 8.8.8.8

# Expected: 0% packet loss


# DNS resolution
nslookup jenkinspreprod.local

# Expected: Correct IP returned


Ansible Connectivity Monitoring:
---------------------------------

# Test Ansible connectivity to all nodes
su - svc_ans -c "ansible all -m ping"

# Expected: SUCCESS for all hosts


# Check Ansible logs
ls -ltr /home/svc_ans/logs/ansible-*/

# Verify recent activity


# Check target node accessibility
for host in 192.168.68.110 192.168.121.164 192.168.121.150 192.168.121.177; do
    echo "Testing $host..."
    ping -c 2 $host > /dev/null && echo "  Ping: OK" || echo "  Ping: FAIL"
    ssh -o BatchMode=yes -o ConnectTimeout=5 svc_ans@$host hostname > /dev/null 2>&1 && echo "  SSH: OK" || echo "  SSH: FAIL"
done


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 14.2: COMMON ISSUES AND SOLUTIONS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Quick resolution guide for common problems

CATEGORIZATION: By symptom and component


CATEGORY 1: JENKINS ISSUES
---------------------------

Issue 1.1: Jenkins Won't Start
-------------------------------

Symptoms:
- systemctl start jenkins fails
- Jenkins service shows "failed" status
- Error in journal logs

Diagnosis:
# Check Jenkins logs
journalctl -u jenkins -n 100 --no-pager

# Check Java is installed
java -version

# Check port 8080 not in use
ss -tlnp | grep 8080

# Check Jenkins home permissions
ls -ld /var/lib/jenkins


Common Causes and Solutions:

A) Java not found or wrong version
   Solution:
   alternatives --config java
   # Select Java 21

B) Port 8080 already in use
   Solution:
   # Find process using port
   ss -tlnp | grep 8080
   # Kill or change Jenkins port

C) Permission issues
   Solution:
   chown -R jenkins:jenkins /var/lib/jenkins
   chmod 750 /var/lib/jenkins

D) Corrupted configuration
   Solution:
   # Restore from backup
   systemctl stop jenkins
   tar xzf /backup/jenkins-ansible-*/jenkins-home.tar.gz -C /
   chown -R jenkins:jenkins /var/lib/jenkins
   systemctl start jenkins


Issue 1.2: Jenkins 502 Bad Gateway
-----------------------------------

Symptoms:
- NGINX shows 502 error
- Cannot access Jenkins UI
- NGINX logs show "upstream" errors

Diagnosis:
# Check if Jenkins is running
systemctl status jenkins

# Check if Jenkins is listening on 8080
ss -tlnp | grep 8080

# Check NGINX can connect to backend
curl http://127.0.0.1:8080

# Check SELinux boolean
getsebool httpd_can_network_connect


Solutions:

A) Jenkins not running
   systemctl start jenkins
   # Wait 30 seconds for startup
   curl http://127.0.0.1:8080

B) SELinux blocking connection
   setsebool -P httpd_can_network_connect 1
   systemctl restart nginx

C) Firewall blocking localhost
   # This shouldn't happen, but verify
   firewall-cmd --list-all

D) NGINX misconfiguration
   nginx -t
   # Fix any errors
   systemctl restart nginx


Issue 1.3: Jenkins Slow or Unresponsive
----------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Jenkins UI loading slowly
- Build queues backing up
- High memory/CPU usage

Diagnosis:
# Check memory usage
free -h
ps aux | grep jenkins

# Check disk space
df -h /var/lib/jenkins

# Check active builds
# Jenkins UI → Manage Jenkins → System Information

# Check Jenkins logs
tail -100 /var/log/jenkins/jenkins.log


Solutions:

A) Insufficient memory
   # Increase Java heap in /etc/systemd/system/jenkins.service.d/override.conf
   # Change -Xmx2048m to -Xmx4096m (if system has enough RAM)
   systemctl daemon-reload
   systemctl restart jenkins

B) Disk space full
   # Clean up old builds
   # Jenkins UI → Manage Jenkins → Disk Usage
   # Or manually:
   find /var/lib/jenkins/jobs -name "builds" -type d -exec du -sh {} \;

C) Too many concurrent builds
   # Limit executors
   # Jenkins UI → Manage Jenkins → Configure System → # of executors

D) Plugin issues
   # Disable problematic plugins
   # Jenkins UI → Manage Jenkins → Plugins
   # Disable recently installed/updated plugins


CATEGORY 2: NGINX ISSUES
-------------------------

Issue 2.1: NGINX Won't Start
-----------------------------

Symptoms:
- systemctl start nginx fails
- nginx -t shows configuration errors

Diagnosis:
nginx -t
journalctl -u nginx -n 50

Common errors:

A) Port 80/443 already in use
   # Find what's using the port
   ss -tlnp | grep :443
   # Stop conflicting service or change NGINX port

B) SSL certificate not found
   # Verify certificate exists
   ls -la /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt
   ls -la /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key
   
   # If missing, restore from backup or regenerate
   openssl req -x509 -nodes -days 3650 ...

C) Configuration syntax error
   nginx -t
   # Read error message carefully
   # Common issues:
   # - Missing semicolon
   # - Unclosed bracket
   # - Invalid directive


Issue 2.2: SSL/TLS Errors
--------------------------

Symptoms:
- Browser shows "Your connection is not private"
- Certificate warnings
- SSL handshake failures

Diagnosis:
# Check certificate validity
openssl x509 -in /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt -noout -dates

# Check certificate matches key
openssl x509 -in /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt -noout -modulus | md5sum
openssl rsa -in /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key -noout -modulus | md5sum
# Both should match


Solutions:

A) Certificate expired
   # Generate new certificate
   openssl req -x509 -nodes -days 3650 \
       -newkey rsa:2048 \
       -keyout /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key \
       -out /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt \
       -subj "/C=IN/ST=Telangana/L=Hyderabad/O=DevOps/CN=jenkinspreprod.local"
   
   systemctl restart nginx

B) Self-signed certificate warning (expected)
   # For production, obtain certificate from trusted CA
   # For testing, instruct users to accept exception

C) Certificate/key mismatch
   # Restore matching pair from backup


CATEGORY 3: ANSIBLE ISSUES
---------------------------

Issue 3.1: "UNREACHABLE" Error
-------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Ansible cannot connect to hosts
- "UNREACHABLE!" in output
- SSH timeout errors

Diagnosis:
# Test SSH manually
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 hostname

# Check firewall on target
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "iptables -L -n | grep 22"

# Check SSH key
ls -la /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa

# Verify key on target
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "cat ~/.ssh/authorized_keys"


Solutions:

A) SSH key not distributed
   ssh-copy-id -i /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa.pub svc_ans@<host>

B) Firewall blocking SSH
   # On Ubuntu targets:
   iptables -A INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -j ACCEPT
   netfilter-persistent save
   
   # On Oracle Linux targets:
   firewall-cmd --permanent --add-service=ssh
   firewall-cmd --reload

C) SSH key permissions wrong
   chmod 600 /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa
   chmod 700 /home/svc_ans/.ssh

D) Host not in known_hosts
   ssh-keyscan <host> >> /home/svc_ans/.ssh/known_hosts


Issue 3.2: "Permission Denied" Error
-------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Tasks fail with permission denied
- Cannot create files
- Cannot install packages

Diagnosis:
# Test sudo manually
ssh svc_ans@<host> "sudo whoami"

# Check sudoers file
ssh svc_ans@<host> "cat /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans"


Solutions:

A) Sudo not configured
   # On target host:
   echo 'svc_ans ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL' > /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans
   chmod 440 /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans
   visudo -cf /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans

B) Become settings incorrect
   # Verify in playbook:
   become: yes
   become_method: sudo
   become_user: root


Issue 3.3: Python Interpreter Not Found
----------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- "/usr/bin/python: not found"
- Interpreter discovery warnings

Diagnosis:
# Check Python on target
ssh svc_ans@<host> "which python3"
ssh svc_ans@<host> "python3 --version"


Solutions:

A) Python not installed
   # On Ubuntu:
   apt install -y python3
   
   # On Oracle Linux:
   dnf install -y python3

B) Interpreter path incorrect in inventory
   # Edit inventory or group_vars
   ansible_python_interpreter=/usr/bin/python3

C) Wrong Python version for OS
   # Ubuntu 22: /usr/bin/python3 (Python 3.10)
   # Ubuntu 24: /usr/bin/python3 (Python 3.12)
   # Oracle 8: /usr/bin/python3.6
   # Oracle 9: /usr/bin/python3.9


Issue 3.4: Ansible 6.7 Not Being Used for Ubuntu 24
----------------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Ubuntu 24 patching fails
- Pipeline uses Ansible 2.9 instead of 6.7

Diagnosis:
# Check Jenkins pipeline console output
# Look for "Using Ansible" message

# Verify virtual environment exists
ls -la /home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/ansible

# Check inventory group
grep -A 5 "\[ubuntu24\]" /home/svc_ans/ansible/hosts


Solutions:

A) Virtual environment not activated
   # Verify pipeline script has venv activation logic
   # Check for:
   if [ "${TARGET_GROUP}" = "ubuntu24" ]; then
       ANSIBLE_BIN="${ANSIBLE_67_BIN}"

B) Inventory group name mismatch
   # Ensure TARGET_GROUP parameter matches inventory
   # Should be exactly: ubuntu24

C) ANSIBLE_VERSION parameter forcing 2.9
   # Change to "auto" or "6.7"


CATEGORY 4: JENKINS PIPELINE ISSUES
------------------------------------

Issue 4.1: Pipeline Fails at "Credentials not found"
-----------------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Pipeline fails in first stage
- Error: "Credentials 'svc_ans_ssh_key' not found"

Solutions:

A) Credential ID mismatch
   # Verify in Jenkins UI:
   # Manage Jenkins → Credentials → System → Global credentials
   # ID must be exactly: svc_ans_ssh_key

B) Credential scope incorrect
   # Credential must have scope "Global"

C) Credential deleted
   # Re-create credential with SSH private key


Issue 4.2: Pipeline Hangs at Approval Stage
--------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Pipeline waits indefinitely at "Approval for Production"
- No one approves

Solutions:

A) Normal behavior - waiting for approval
   # Click "Yes, Execute Patching" in Jenkins UI

B) Timeout configured
   # Default: 30 minutes
   # Adjust timeout in pipeline script if needed

C) Submitter restriction
   # Pipeline may require specific user to approve
   # Check submitter: setting in input step


Issue 4.3: Ansible Command Not Found in Pipeline
-------------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Error: "ansible: command not found"
- Pipeline fails during Ansible execution

Diagnosis:
# Check paths in pipeline environment variables
# Verify:
ANSIBLE_29_BIN=/usr/bin/ansible
ANSIBLE_67_BIN=/home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/ansible


Solutions:

A) Ansible not installed
   # System Ansible:
   dnf install -y ansible
   
   # Venv Ansible:
   python3.11 -m venv /home/svc_ans/ansible-venv
   /home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/pip install ansible==6.7.0

B) Path incorrect in pipeline
   # Verify actual locations:
   which ansible
   ls -la /home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/ansible
   
   # Update pipeline environment variables


CATEGORY 5: FIREWALL ISSUES
----------------------------

Issue 5.1: Cannot Access Jenkins HTTPS
---------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- Cannot connect to https://jenkinspreprod.local
- Connection timeout
- Connection refused

Diagnosis:
# Check firewall allows HTTPS
firewall-cmd --list-services | grep https

# Check NGINX is listening
ss -tlnp | grep :443

# Check from localhost
curl -k https://localhost


Solutions:

A) Firewall blocking HTTPS
   firewall-cmd --permanent --add-service=https
   firewall-cmd --reload

B) NGINX not running
   systemctl start nginx

C) NGINX not listening on 443
   # Check /etc/nginx/conf.d/jenkins.conf
   # Should have: listen 443 ssl http2;


Issue 5.2: iptables Rules Lost After Reboot (Ubuntu)
-----------------------------------------------------

Symptoms:
- After reboot, cannot connect to Ubuntu nodes
- iptables rules empty

Diagnosis:
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "iptables -L -n"


Solutions:

A) netfilter-persistent not enabled
   ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "systemctl enable netfilter-persistent"

B) Rules not saved
   ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "netfilter-persistent save"

C) /etc/iptables/rules.v4 missing
   # Recreate rules (see Part 4)
   # Save with: netfilter-persistent save

SECTION 14.3: DIAGNOSTIC COMMANDS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Quick diagnostic commands for troubleshooting

CATEGORIZATION: By component


JENKINS DIAGNOSTICS:
--------------------

# Service status
systemctl status jenkins

# Port check
ss -tlnp | grep 8080

# Java process
ps aux | grep jenkins | grep -v grep

# Memory usage
ps aux | grep jenkins | awk '{print $6/1024 " MB"}'

# Recent logs
journalctl -u jenkins -n 100 --no-pager

# Recent errors
journalctl -u jenkins | grep -i error | tail -20

# Configuration test
# (No direct test, but check config.xml)
head -20 /var/lib/jenkins/config.xml

# Disk usage
du -sh /var/lib/jenkins
du -sh /var/lib/jenkins/jobs

# Build history
ls -ltr /var/lib/jenkins/jobs/*/builds/ | tail -20


NGINX DIAGNOSTICS:
------------------

# Service status
systemctl status nginx

# Configuration test
nginx -t

# Port check
ss -tlnp | grep nginx

# Process check
ps aux | grep nginx | grep -v grep

# Recent access logs
tail -50 /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log

# Recent error logs
tail -50 /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log

# Error count
grep -c error /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log

# 502 errors
grep " 502 " /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log | tail -10

# Active connections
ss -s

# Test HTTPS
curl -k -I https://localhost


ANSIBLE DIAGNOSTICS:
--------------------

# Version check (system)
/usr/bin/ansible --version

# Version check (venv)
/home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/ansible --version

# Inventory list
ansible all --list-hosts

# Connectivity test
ansible all -m ping

# Verbose connectivity
ansible all -m ping -vvv

# Check Python on targets
ansible all -m shell -a "which python3 && python3 --version"

# Check disk on targets
ansible all -m shell -a "df -h /"

# Check uptime on targets
ansible all -m shell -a "uptime"

# Playbook syntax check
ansible-playbook /etc/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --syntax-check

# Playbook dry run
ansible-playbook /etc/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --check --limit ubuntu22


SYSTEM DIAGNOSTICS:
-------------------

# CPU usage
top -bn1 | head -20

# Memory usage
free -h

# Disk space
df -h

# Disk I/O
iostat -x 1 3

# Network connectivity
ping -c 4 8.8.8.8

# DNS resolution
nslookup jenkinspreprod.local

# Firewall status
firewall-cmd --state
firewall-cmd --list-all

# SELinux status
getenforce
getsebool httpd_can_network_connect

# Time sync
timedatectl status

# System load
uptime

# Recent logins
last -10

# Failed login attempts
lastb -10

# Open files
lsof | wc -l

# Zombie processes
ps aux | grep defunct


SSH DIAGNOSTICS:
----------------

# Test SSH to host
ssh -v svc_ans@192.168.68.110 hostname

# Check SSH key
ls -la /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa
ssh-keygen -l -f /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa

# Check authorized_keys on target
ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 "cat ~/.ssh/authorized_keys"

# Test batch mode (no prompts)
ssh -o BatchMode=yes svc_ans@192.168.68.110 hostname

# Check known_hosts
cat /home/svc_ans/.ssh/known_hosts | wc -l


PERFORMANCE DIAGNOSTICS:
-------------------------

# System load average
uptime

# Process tree
pstree -p

# Top processes by CPU
ps aux --sort=-%cpu | head -10

# Top processes by memory
ps aux --sort=-%mem | head -10

# Network statistics
netstat -s

# Connection states
ss -s

# Bandwidth usage (if iftop installed)
# iftop -i eth0


LOG ANALYSIS COMMANDS:
----------------------

# Jenkins logs - last hour
journalctl -u jenkins --since "1 hour ago"

# Jenkins errors today
journalctl -u jenkins --since today | grep -i error

# NGINX errors last 24h
find /var/log/nginx -name "*.log" -mtime -1 -exec grep -i error {} \;

# System logs critical
journalctl -p err -since today

# Kernel messages
dmesg | tail -50

# Disk errors
dmesg | grep -i "error"

# OOM killer events
grep -i "out of memory" /var/log/messages

SECTION 14.4: EMERGENCY CONTACTS AND ESCALATION
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Define support structure and escalation path


SUPPORT TIERS:
--------------

Level 1: Operations Team (First Response)
- Email: ops-team@example.com
- Slack: #operations-support
- Phone: +1-555-0100 (24/7 hotline)
- Response Time: 15 minutes
- Scope: Service restarts, basic troubleshooting, known issues


Level 2: Infrastructure Team (Advanced Support)
- Email: infrastructure-team@example.com
- Slack: #infrastructure-escalation
- Phone: +1-555-0200 (Business hours)
- Response Time: 1 hour
- Scope: Configuration changes, complex issues, root cause analysis


Level 3: Automation Team (Expert Support)
- Email: automation-team@example.com
- Slack: #automation-experts
- Phone: +1-555-0300 (On-call rotation)
- Response Time: 2 hours
- Scope: Ansible playbook issues, pipeline development, architecture


Level 4: Senior Architect (Strategic)
- Email: senior-architect@example.com
- Phone: +1-555-0400 (Emergency only)
- Response Time: 4 hours
- Scope: Architecture decisions, disaster recovery, major incidents


External Vendors:
-----------------

Red Hat Ansible Support:
- Portal: https://access.redhat.com
- Phone: Per support contract
- Severity Levels: Critical, High, Medium, Low
- SLA: Based on severity and contract

Jenkins Community:
- IRC: #jenkins on Libera.Chat
- Mailing List: jenkinsci-users@googlegroups.com
- Website: https://www.jenkins.io/participate/


ESCALATION CRITERIA:
--------------------

Escalate to Level 2 if:
- Issue not resolved in 30 minutes
- Service impact to multiple users
- Security concern identified
- Data loss suspected

Escalate to Level 3 if:
- Issue not resolved in 2 hours
- Ansible automation broken
- Pipeline development needed
- Architecture question

Escalate to Level 4 if:
- Business-critical outage
- Data breach suspected
- Disaster recovery needed
- Executive stakeholder involved


INCIDENT SEVERITY LEVELS:
--------------------------

Severity 1 (Critical):
- Jenkins completely unavailable
- Multiple systems affected
- Business-critical automation broken
- Security breach
- Response: Immediate (15 minutes)
- Updates: Every 30 minutes

Severity 2 (High):
- Jenkins degraded performance
- Single system impacted
- Non-critical automation broken
- Response: 1 hour
- Updates: Every 2 hours

Severity 3 (Medium):
- Minor functionality issue
- Workaround available
- Single user impacted
- Response: 4 hours
- Updates: Daily

Severity 4 (Low):
- Feature request
- Question or guidance
- Documentation issue
- Response: Best effort
- Updates: As needed

Subject: [SEV-X] Brief description of issue

SUMMARY:
<One-line description>

IMPACT:
<Systems affected, users impacted, business impact>

CURRENT STATUS:
<What's working, what's not, current state>

ACTIONS TAKEN:
<What has been tried, results>

NEXT STEPS:
<Planned actions, ETR>

CONTACT:
<Your name, phone, email>

SECTION 15.2: CRITICAL COMMANDS

PURPOSE: Essential commands for daily operations


JENKINS COMMANDS:
-----------------

cat /var/lib/jenkins/secrets/initialAdminPassword


NGINX COMMANDS:
---------------

systemctl status nginx
systemctl start nginx
systemctl stop nginx

systemctl reload nginx  # Reload config without dropping connections

# Configuration

nginx -T  # Test and dump configuration

tail -f /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log
tail -f /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log
tail -50 /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log | grep " 502 "  # Find 502 errors

ansible-playbook /etc/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --check
ansible-playbook /etc/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --limit ubuntu22

ansible-playbook ~/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --check

deactivate


SSH COMMANDS:

ssh svc_ans@192.168.68.110 hostname
ssh svc_ans@192.168.121.164 hostname
ssh svc_ans@192.168.121.150 hostname
ssh svc_ans@192.168.121.177 hostname

# Batch test all hosts
for host in 192.168.68.110 192.168.121.164 192.168.121.150 192.168.121.177; do
    echo "Testing $host..."
    ssh -o BatchMode=yes -o ConnectTimeout=5 svc_ans@$host "hostname && sudo whoami"
done

# Copy SSH key to new host
ssh-copy-id -i /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa.pub svc_ans@<new-host>

# Add host to known_hosts
ssh-keyscan <host> >> /home/svc_ans/.ssh/known_hosts
ssh-keyscan <host> >> /var/lib/jenkins/.ssh/known_hosts

./RESTORE.sh

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 15.3: SERVICE MANAGEMENT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Standard service operations


START SERVICES:
---------------

# Start all services
systemctl start jenkins
systemctl start nginx
systemctl start firewalld
systemctl start fail2ban

# Start in order (recommended)
systemctl start firewalld
sleep 2
systemctl start jenkins
sleep 30  # Wait for Jenkins to fully start
systemctl start nginx


STOP SERVICES:
--------------

# Stop all services
systemctl stop nginx
systemctl stop jenkins
# Don't stop firewalld (security risk)

# Stop in order (recommended)
systemctl stop nginx
sleep 5
systemctl stop jenkins


RESTART SERVICES:
-----------------

# Restart Jenkins (drops active sessions)
systemctl restart jenkins

# Restart NGINX (minimal disruption)
systemctl reload nginx  # Preferred
# OR
systemctl restart nginx


ENABLE SERVICES (START ON BOOT):
---------------------------------

systemctl enable jenkins
systemctl enable nginx
systemctl enable firewalld
systemctl enable fail2ban
systemctl enable chronyd


CHECK SERVICE STATUS:
---------------------

# Individual status
systemctl status jenkins
systemctl status nginx
systemctl status firewalld

# All at once
systemctl status jenkins nginx firewalld fail2ban


VERIFY SERVICES ENABLED:
------------------------

systemctl is-enabled jenkins
systemctl is-enabled nginx
systemctl is-enabled firewalld

# Expected: "enabled" for all

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 15.5: COMMON TASKS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Step-by-step guides for frequent operations


TASK 1: Execute OS Patching
---------------------------

1. Access Jenkins:
   https://jenkinspreprod.local

2. Click: "Linux-OS-Patching-Unified"

3. Click: "Build with Parameters"

4. Select parameters:
   - TARGET_GROUP: ubuntu22 (or desired group)
   - ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
   - DRY_RUN: true (for safety check)
   - REBOOT_ALLOWED: true

5. Click: "Build"

6. Monitor console output

7. If dry run successful, run again with:
   - DRY_RUN: false
   - Click "Build"
   - Approve when prompted

8. Verify completion in console output


TASK 2: Add New Managed Host
-----------------------------

1. Prepare new host:
   # Create svc_ans user
   useradd -m -s /bin/bash svc_ans
   passwd svc_ans
   usermod -aG sudo svc_ans  # Ubuntu
   usermod -aG wheel svc_ans  # Oracle Linux
   
   # Configure passwordless sudo
   echo 'svc_ans ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL' > /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans
   chmod 440 /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans
   
   # Configure firewall to allow SSH
   # (See Part 4 for details)

2. From control node as svc_ans:
   # Copy SSH key
   ssh-copy-id -i ~/.ssh/id_rsa.pub svc_ans@<new-host>
   
   # Add to known_hosts
   ssh-keyscan <new-host> >> ~/.ssh/known_hosts
   ssh-keyscan <new-host-ip> >> ~/.ssh/known_hosts
   
   # Test connection
   ssh svc_ans@<new-host> "hostname && sudo whoami"

3. Add to Jenkins known_hosts:
   ssh-keyscan <new-host> >> /var/lib/jenkins/.ssh/known_hosts

4. Add to Ansible inventory:
   vi /home/svc_ans/ansible/hosts
   
   # Add under appropriate group:
   [ubuntu24]
   192.168.121.164
   <new-host-ip>  # Add here
   
   # Save and exit

5. Test Ansible connectivity:
   ansible <new-host-ip> -m ping

6. Run test playbook:
   ansible-playbook ~/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml \
       --limit <new-host-ip> \
       --check


TASK 3: Update SSL Certificate
-------------------------------

1. Generate new certificate:
   openssl req -x509 -nodes -days 3650 \
       -newkey rsa:2048 \
       -keyout /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key.new \
       -out /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt.new \
       -subj "/C=IN/ST=Telangana/L=Hyderabad/O=DevOps/CN=jenkinspreprod.local"

2. Backup old certificates:
   cp /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key.bak
   cp /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt.bak

3. Replace certificates:
   mv /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key.new /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key
   mv /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt.new /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt
   
   chmod 600 /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key
   chmod 644 /etc/ssl/certs/jenkins.crt

4. Test NGINX configuration:
   nginx -t

5. Reload NGINX:
   systemctl reload nginx

6. Verify:
   curl -k -I https://jenkinspreprod.local


TASK 4: Restore from Backup
---------------------------

CAUTION: This overwrites current configuration

1. Stop services:
   systemctl stop nginx
   systemctl stop jenkins

2. Navigate to backup:
   cd /backup/jenkins-ansible-daily-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/

3. Review manifest:
   cat MANIFEST.txt

4. Execute restore:
   ./RESTORE.sh

5. Follow prompts (type "yes" to confirm)

6. Wait for restore to complete

7. Verify services:
   systemctl status jenkins nginx

8. Test access:
   https://jenkinspreprod.local


TASK 5: Update Ansible Playbook
-------------------------------

1. Edit playbook:
   vi /home/svc_ans/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml

2. Make changes

3. Test syntax:
   ansible-playbook ~/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml --syntax-check

4. Dry run:
   ansible-playbook ~/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml \
       --check \
       --limit ubuntu22

5. If successful, copy to system location:
   cp /home/svc_ans/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml \
      /etc/ansible/playbooks/os_patching_unified.yml

6. Test via Jenkins pipeline with DRY_RUN=true


TASK 6: View Logs
----------------

Jenkins Logs:
journalctl -u jenkins -f

NGINX Access Logs:
tail -f /var/log/nginx/jenkins.access.log

NGINX Error Logs:
tail -f /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log

Ansible Logs (on targets):
ssh svc_ans@<host> "ls -ltr /var/log/ansible-patching/"
ssh svc_ans@<host> "cat /var/log/ansible-patching/patching_YYYY-MM-DD.log"

Backup Logs:
tail -f /var/log/backup-jenkins-ansible.log

All Jenkins Errors Today:
journalctl -u jenkins --since today | grep -i error


TASK 7: Restart All Services (Maintenance)
------------------------------------------

1. Notify users of maintenance window

2. Stop NGINX (stops incoming requests):
   systemctl stop nginx

3. Wait for active builds to complete (check Jenkins UI)

4. Stop Jenkins:
   systemctl stop jenkins

5. Wait 30 seconds:
   sleep 30

6. Start Jenkins:
   systemctl start jenkins

7. Wait for Jenkins to start (check logs):
   journalctl -u jenkins -f
   # Wait for "Jenkins is fully up and running"

8. Test Jenkins locally:
   curl http://127.0.0.1:8080

9. Start NGINX:
   systemctl start nginx

10. Test external access:
    curl -k -I https://jenkinspreprod.local

11. Notify users maintenance complete

SECTION 15.6: INVENTORY GROUPS REFERENCE
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Quick lookup for inventory groups


PRIMARY GROUPS:
---------------

[ubuntu22]
- 192.168.68.110 (ubuntu22.local)
- Uses Ansible 2.9
- Python: /usr/bin/python3

[ubuntu24]
- 192.168.121.164 (ubuntu24.local)
- Uses Ansible 6.7 (venv)
- Python: /usr/bin/python3

[oracle8]
- 192.168.121.150 (oracle8.local)
- Uses Ansible 2.9
- Python: /usr/bin/python3.6

[oracle9]
- 192.168.121.177 (oracle9.local)
- Uses Ansible 2.9
- Python: /usr/bin/python3.9


LOGICAL GROUPS:
---------------

[ubuntu:children]
- ubuntu22
- ubuntu24

[oracle:children]
- oracle8
- oracle9

[all_linux:children]
- ubuntu
- oracle


ANSIBLE VERSION GROUPS:
-----------------------

[ansible_2_9:children]
- ubuntu22
- oracle8
- oracle9

[ansible_6_7:children]
- ubuntu24


USING GROUPS IN COMMANDS:
--------------------------

# Target specific group
ansible ubuntu22 -m ping
ansible ubuntu24 -m ping
ansible oracle8 -m ping

# Target logical group
ansible ubuntu -m ping
ansible oracle -m ping

# Target all
ansible all -m ping

# Target multiple groups
ansible ubuntu22,oracle8 -m ping

# Exclude group
ansible all:!ubuntu24 -m ping


USING GROUPS IN PLAYBOOKS:
---------------------------

# In playbook
- name: Patch Ubuntu systems only
  hosts: ubuntu
  become: yes
  tasks:
    - ...

# In Jenkins pipeline --limit parameter
--limit ubuntu22
--limit ubuntu24
--limit ubuntu
--limit all_linux


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 15.7: ANSIBLE VERSION SELECTION GUIDE
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Quick decision guide for Ansible version


AUTOMATIC SELECTION (RECOMMENDED):
-----------------------------------

In Jenkins Pipeline:
- Set ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
- Pipeline automatically selects based on TARGET_GROUP
- Ubuntu 24 → Ansible 6.7
- All others → Ansible 2.9


MANUAL SELECTION:
-----------------

Use Ansible 2.9 (System):
-------------------------

When:
- Targeting Ubuntu 22
- Targeting Oracle Linux 8
- Targeting Oracle Linux 9
- Running legacy playbooks

Command Line:
/usr/bin/ansible-playbook <playbook>

Jenkins Parameter:
ANSIBLE_VERSION: 2.9


Use Ansible 6.7 (Venv):
-----------------------

When:
- Targeting Ubuntu 24
- Need modern features
- Testing new playbooks

Command Line:
source /home/svc_ans/ansible-venv/bin/activate
ansible-playbook <playbook>
deactivate

Jenkins Parameter:
ANSIBLE_VERSION: 6.7


VERSION COMPATIBILITY:
----------------------

Playbook Feature              | Ansible 2.9 | Ansible 6.7
------------------------------|-------------|-------------
apt module                    | ✓           | ✓
dnf module                    | ✓           | ✓
yum module                    | ✓           | ✓
service module                | ✓           | ✓
systemd module                | ✓           | ✓
copy module                   | ✓           | ✓
file module                   | ✓           | ✓
shell module                  | ✓           | ✓
reboot module                 | ✓           | ✓
wait_for_connection module    | ✓           | ✓
community.general collection  | Limited     | ✓
ansible.posix collection      | Limited     | ✓
Ubuntu 24 Python 3.12         | ✗           | ✓


TROUBLESHOOTING VERSION ISSUES:
--------------------------------

Issue: Ubuntu 24 fails with Ansible 2.9
Solution: Use Ansible 6.7 or set ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto

Issue: Module not found
Solution: Install collections in venv:
  source ~/ansible-venv/bin/activate
  ansible-galaxy collection install community.general

Issue: Python interpreter error
Solution: Set correct interpreter in group_vars


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 15.8: JENKINS PIPELINE PARAMETERS
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Quick reference for pipeline parameters


PARAMETER: TARGET_GROUP
-----------------------

Type: Choice
Values: all_linux, ubuntu, oracle, ubuntu22, ubuntu24, oracle8, oracle9

Purpose: Select which hosts to patch

Examples:
- ubuntu22: Patch only Ubuntu 22 hosts
- ubuntu24: Patch only Ubuntu 24 hosts
- ubuntu: Patch all Ubuntu hosts (22 + 24)
- oracle: Patch all Oracle Linux hosts (8 + 9)
- all_linux: Patch all hosts


PARAMETER: ANSIBLE_VERSION
---------------------------

Type: Choice
Values: auto, 2.9, 6.7

Purpose: Select Ansible version or auto-detect

Recommendations:
- auto: Recommended (automatically selects based on target)
- 2.9: Force Ansible 2.9 (for troubleshooting)
- 6.7: Force Ansible 6.7 (for troubleshooting or testing)


PARAMETER: DRY_RUN
------------------

Type: Boolean
Default: true

Purpose: Run in check mode (no changes applied)

Usage:
- true: Dry run (safe, shows what would change)
- false: Production run (applies changes)

Recommendation: Always run with DRY_RUN=true first


PARAMETER: REBOOT_ALLOWED
--------------------------

Type: Boolean
Default: true

Purpose: Allow automatic reboot if required

Usage:
- true: Reboot automatically if updates require it
- false: Skip reboot even if required

Note: If false, manual reboot needed later


PARAMETER: LIMIT_HOSTS
-----------------------

Type: String
Default: (empty)

Purpose: Limit to specific hosts (optional)

Examples:
- Empty: Use TARGET_GROUP
- 192.168.68.110: Single host
- 192.168.68.110,192.168.121.164: Multiple hosts
- ubuntu22-web01: By hostname (if in inventory)


PARAMETER: EXTRA_VARS
----------------------

Type: String
Default: (empty)

Purpose: Pass extra variables to playbook

Examples:
- security_updates_only=true
- reboot_after_patch=false
- patch_log_dir=/var/log/custom

Format: key1=value1 key2=value2


PARAMETER: TAGS
---------------

Type: String
Default: (empty)

Purpose: Run only specific playbook sections

Examples:
- patching: Run only patching tasks
- verification: Run only verification tasks
- patching,logging: Run multiple tags


COMMON PARAMETER COMBINATIONS:
-------------------------------

Safe Dry Run on Ubuntu 22:
- TARGET_GROUP: ubuntu22
- ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
- DRY_RUN: true
- REBOOT_ALLOWED: true

Production Patch Ubuntu 24:
- TARGET_GROUP: ubuntu24
- ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
- DRY_RUN: false
- REBOOT_ALLOWED: true

Patch Single Host Without Reboot:
- TARGET_GROUP: ubuntu22
- ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
- DRY_RUN: false
- REBOOT_ALLOWED: false
- LIMIT_HOSTS: 192.168.68.110

Emergency Patch All:
- TARGET_GROUP: all_linux
- ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto
- DRY_RUN: false
- REBOOT_ALLOWED: true


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 15.9: TROUBLESHOOTING QUICK REFERENCE
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

PURPOSE: Fast symptom-to-solution lookup


SYMPTOM: Cannot Access Jenkins UI
----------------------------------

Check:
1. systemctl status jenkins
2. systemctl status nginx
3. curl -k https://jenkinspreprod.local
4. firewall-cmd --list-services | grep https

Fix:
systemctl start jenkins nginx
firewall-cmd --permanent --add-service=https
firewall-cmd --reload


SYMPTOM: 502 Bad Gateway
-------------------------

Check:
1. systemctl status jenkins
2. ss -tlnp | grep 8080
3. getsebool httpd_can_network_connect

Fix:
systemctl start jenkins
setsebool -P httpd_can_network_connect 1
systemctl restart nginx


SYMPTOM: Ansible UNREACHABLE
-----------------------------

Check:
1. ssh svc_ans@<host> hostname
2. ansible <host> -m ping -vvv
3. iptables/firewall rules on target

Fix:
ssh-copy-id svc_ans@<host>
ssh-keyscan <host> >> ~/.ssh/known_hosts
# Fix firewall on target


SYMPTOM: Permission Denied
---------------------------

Check:
1. ssh svc_ans@<host> "sudo whoami"
2. ssh svc_ans@<host> "cat /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans"

Fix:
echo 'svc_ans ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL' > /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans
chmod 440 /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans


SYMPTOM: Python Not Found
--------------------------

Check:
ssh svc_ans@<host> "which python3"

Fix:
# On Ubuntu:
apt install -y python3

# On Oracle Linux:
dnf install -y python3

# Update inventory with correct path


SYMPTOM: Pipeline Fails - Credentials Not Found
------------------------------------------------

Check:
Jenkins → Manage Jenkins → Credentials
Look for: svc_ans_ssh_key

Fix:
Re-create credential with exact ID: svc_ans_ssh_key


SYMPTOM: Ubuntu 24 Fails with Ansible 2.9
------------------------------------------

Check:
Jenkins console output for "Using Ansible" message

Fix:
Set ANSIBLE_VERSION: auto or 6.7


SYMPTOM: Backup Failed
----------------------

Check:
1. df -h /backup
2. tail -50 /var/log/backup-jenkins-ansible.log

Fix:
# Free up space
# OR
# Change BACKUP_BASE_DIR in backup script


SYMPTOM: Service Won't Start After Reboot
------------------------------------------

Check:
1. systemctl is-enabled jenkins
2. systemctl is-enabled nginx

Fix:
systemctl enable jenkins nginx firewalld
systemctl start jenkins nginx


SYMPTOM: Firewall Rules Lost After Reboot (Ubuntu)
---------------------------------------------------

Check:
ssh svc_ans@<ubuntu-host> "iptables -L -n"

Fix:
ssh svc_ans@<ubuntu-host> "systemctl enable netfilter-persistent"
ssh svc_ans@<ubuntu-host> "netfilter-persistent save"

APPENDIX B: SECURITY HARDENING CHECKLIST
================================================================================

NETWORK SECURITY:
-----------------

[ ] Firewall enabled on all nodes
[ ] Only required ports open (22, 443)
[ ] SSH restricted to specific networks (optional)
[ ] Fail2ban active on control node
[ ] Rate limiting configured in NGINX
[ ] SELinux enabled and enforcing


ACCESS CONTROL:
---------------

[ ] Service account (svc_ans) with minimal privileges
[ ] SSH key-based authentication only (no passwords)
[ ] Passwordless sudo configured securely
[ ] Jenkins authentication required (LDAP or local)
[ ] Matrix-based authorization in Jenkins
[ ] Regular audit of user permissions


ENCRYPTION:
-----------

[ ] HTTPS enforced (HTTP dropped with 444)
[ ] TLS 1.2 and 1.3 only
[ ] Strong cipher suites configured
[ ] HSTS header enabled
[ ] SSH keys 4096-bit RSA
[ ] Sensitive backups encrypted


FILE PERMISSIONS:
-----------------

[ ] /home/svc_ans/.ssh/id_rsa: 600
[ ] /home/svc_ans/.ssh: 700
[ ] /etc/ssl/private/jenkins.key: 600
[ ] /etc/sudoers.d/svc_ans: 440
[ ] /var/lib/jenkins: 750 jenkins:jenkins
[ ] Backup directories: 700

APPENDIX C: TROUBLESHOOTING FLOWCHART
================================================================================

JENKINS NOT ACCESSIBLE:
-----------------------

START → Can you ping control node?
        │
        ├─ NO → Check network connectivity
        │       Check firewall rules
        │       Check DNS resolution
        │
        └─ YES → Can you access https://jenkinspreprod.local?
                 │
                 ├─ NO → Is NGINX running?
                 │       │
                 │       ├─ NO → systemctl start nginx
                 │       │
                 │       └─ YES → Is Jenkins running?
                 │                │
                 │                ├─ NO → systemctl start jenkins
                 │                │
                 │                └─ YES → Check SELinux boolean
                 │                         Check NGINX config
                 │                         Check /var/log/nginx/jenkins.error.log
                 │
                 └─ YES → Is UI slow?
                          │
                          ├─ YES → Check memory usage
                          │        Check disk space
                          │        Check active builds
                          │
                          └─ NO → Success!


ANSIBLE PLAYBOOK FAILS:
-----------------------

START → Does playbook syntax check pass?
        │
        ├─ NO → ansible-playbook <playbook> --syntax-check
        │       Fix syntax errors
        │
        └─ YES → Can Ansible ping hosts?
                 │
                 ├─ NO → Is SSH working?
                 │       │
                 │       ├─ NO → Check SSH keys
                 │       │       Check firewall on target
                 │       │       ssh svc_ans@<host> hostname
                 │       │
                 │       └─ YES → Check Ansible inventory
                 │                Check Python on target
                 │
                 └─ YES → Does playbook fail on specific task?
                          │
                          ├─ YES → Check task error message
                          │        Check become/sudo permissions
                          │        Check module compatibility
                          │        Run with -vvv for details
                          │
                          └─ NO → Playbook succeeds!


PIPELINE EXECUTION ISSUES:
--------------------------

START → Does pipeline start?
        │
        ├─ NO → Is Jenkins running?
        │       Check job exists
        │       Check user permissions
        │
        └─ YES → Which stage fails?
                 │
                 ├─ Environment Validation → Check Ansible binaries
                 │                           Check inventory file
                 │                           Check playbook file
                 │
                 ├─ Connectivity Test → Check SSH connectivity
                 │                      Check firewall rules
                 │                      Check Ansible ping
                 │
                 ├─ Dry Run → Check playbook syntax
                 │            Check Python interpreter
                 │            Check become permissions
                 │
                 ├─ Execute Patching → Check approval given
                 │                     Check disk space on targets
                 │                     Check network stability
                 │
                 └─ Post-Patch Verification → Check hosts came back online
                                              Check services running

Knowledge Base: https://kb.internal.company.com


================================================================================
END OF COMPLETE DOCUMENTATION
================================================================================

PART 11: LDAP INTEGRATION
11.1 Install LDAP Plugin
Via Jenkins Web UI:
Navigate to Jenkins Dashboard
Click "Manage Jenkins" → "Manage Plugins"
Go to "Available" tab
Search for "LDAP"
Select "LDAP Plugin"
Click "Install without restart" or "Download now and install after restart"

# Install LDAP plugin
java -jar jenkins-cli.jar -s http://localhost:8080/ install-plugin ldap

# Restart Jenkins
java -jar jenkins-cli.jar -s http://localhost:8080/ safe-restart


# Install LDAP plugin
RUN jenkins-plugin-cli --plugins ldap:latest

Verify Installation:
Go to "Manage Jenkins" → "Manage Plugins" → "Installed" tab
Search for "LDAP"
Confirm "LDAP Plugin" is listed


# Example Configuration Values

# Active Directory Configuration:
Server: ldap://ad.company.com:389
Root DN: DC=company,DC=com
User search base: CN=Users,DC=company,DC=com
User search filter: (& (sAMAccountName={0}) (objectClass=user))
Group search base: CN=Groups,DC=company,DC=com
Group search filter: (& (cn={0}) (objectclass=group))
Group membership attribute: member

# OpenLDAP Configuration:
Server: ldap://openldap.company.com:389
Root DN: dc=company,dc=com
User search base: ou=People,dc=company,dc=com
User search filter: (uid={0})
Group search base: ou=Groups,dc=company,dc=com
Group search filter: (cn={0})
Group membership attribute: memberUid

# Display Name LDAP Attribute: displayName (or cn)
# Email Address LDAP Attribute: mail
